<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Degenerate energy levels</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about different quantum states having the same energy. For other uses, see <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Degeneracy_(disambiguation)" title="Degeneracy (disambiguation)">Degeneracy</a>.</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Quantum degeneracy" redirects here. It sometimes refers to a <a href="/wiki/Degenerate_matter" title="Degenerate matter">degenerate matter</a>.</div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(February 2009)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Energy_level" title="Energy level">energy level</a> is <b>degenerate</b> if it corresponds to two or more different measurable states of a <a href="/wiki/Quantum_system" title="Quantum system">quantum system</a>. Conversely, two or more different states of a quantum mechanical system are said to be degenerate if they give the same value of energy upon measurement. The number of different states corresponding to a particular energy level is known as the degree of degeneracy of the level. It is represented mathematically by the <a href="/wiki/Hamiltonian_(quantum_mechanics)" title="Hamiltonian (quantum mechanics)">Hamiltonian</a> for the system having more than one <a href="/wiki/Linear_independence" title="Linear independence">linearly independent</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eigenstate" title="Eigenstate">eigenstate</a> with the same energy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eigenvalue" title="Eigenvalue">eigenvalue</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merzbacher98_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merzbacher98-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 48</span></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">classical mechanics</a>, this can be understood in terms of different possible trajectories corresponding to the same energy.
</p><p>Degeneracy plays a fundamental role in <a href="/wiki/Quantum_statistical_mechanics" title="Quantum statistical mechanics">quantum statistical mechanics</a>. For an <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">N</span>-particle system in three dimensions, a single energy level may correspond to several different wave functions or energy states. These degenerate states at the same level are all equally probable of being filled. The number of such states gives the degeneracy of a particular energy level.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Degenerate_energy_levels.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="398" data-file-width="506" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Degenerate_energy_levels.svg/330px-Degenerate_energy_levels.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Degenerate_energy_levels.svg/495px-Degenerate_energy_levels.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Degenerate_energy_levels.svg/660px-Degenerate_energy_levels.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Degenerate_energy_levels.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Degenerate states in a quantum system</div></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mathematics">Mathematics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Mathematics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(January 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The possible states of a quantum mechanical system may be treated mathematically as abstract vectors in a separable, complex <a href="/wiki/Hilbert_space" title="Hilbert space">Hilbert space</a>, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Observables" title="Observables">observables</a> may be represented by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linear_operator" title="Linear operator">linear</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hermitian_operator" title="Hermitian operator">Hermitian operators</a> acting upon them. By selecting a suitable <a href="/wiki/Basis_function" title="Basis function">basis</a>, the components of these vectors and the matrix elements of the operators in that basis may be determined. 
If <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">A</span> is a <span class="texhtml"><i>N</i> × <i>N</i></span> matrix, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> a non-zero <a href="/wiki/Euclidean_vector" title="Euclidean vector">vector</a>, and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">λ</span> is a <a href="/wiki/Scalar_(physics)" title="Scalar (physics)">scalar</a>, such that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle AX=\lambda X}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>A</mi>
<mi>X</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>λ<!-- λ --></mi>
<mi>X</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle AX=\lambda X}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="AX=\lambda X" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e4510147ebc492c912b59778493d9fc66b0e6506" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:10.157ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, then the scalar <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">λ</span> is said to be an eigenvalue of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">A</span> and the vector <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> is said to be the eigenvector corresponding to <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;"> λ</span>. Together with the zero vector, the set of all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eigenvectors" title="Eigenvectors">eigenvectors</a> corresponding to a given eigenvalue <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">λ</span> form a <a href="/wiki/Subspace_topology" title="Subspace topology">subspace</a> of <span class="texhtml"><b>C</b><sup><i>n</i></sup></span>, which is called the <b>eigenspace</b> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">λ</span>. An eigenvalue <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">λ</span> which corresponds to two or more different linearly independent eigenvectors is said to be <b>degenerate</b>, i.e., <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle AX_{1}=\lambda X_{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>A</mi>
<msub>
<mi>X</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>λ<!-- λ --></mi>
<msub>
<mi>X</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle AX_{1}=\lambda X_{1}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="AX_{1}=\lambda X_{1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6c4c5e19edfbe295906778d08cb38e9d03d62e9d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.154ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle AX_{2}=\lambda X_{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle AX_{2}=\lambda X_{2}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="AX_{2}=\lambda X_{2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/44766b229c86d0427a973c94cd11fe3b5dadda73" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.154ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X_{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>X</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X_{1}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="X_{1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f70b2694445a5901b24338a2e7a7e58f02a72a32" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.979ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X_{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>X</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X_{2}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="X_{2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2ad47c14b8a092f182512e76c96638aea6e3bea1" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.979ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> are linearly independent eigenvectors.The dimensionality of the eigenspace corresponding to that eigenvalue is known as its <b>degree of degeneracy</b>, which can be finite or infinite. An eigenvalue is said to be non-degenerate if its eigenspace is one-dimensional.
The eigenvalues of the matrices representing physical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Observables" title="Observables">observables</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a> give the measurable values of these observables while the eigenstates corresponding to these eigenvalues give the possible states in which the system may be found, upon measurement. The measurable values of the energy of a quantum system are given by the eigenvalues of the Hamiltonian operator, while its eigenstates give the possible energy states of the system. A value of energy is said to be degenerate if there exist at least two linearly independent energy states associated with it. Moreover, any <a href="/wiki/Linear_combination" title="Linear combination">linear combination</a> of two or more degenerate eigenstates is also an eigenstate of the Hamiltonian operator corresponding to the same energy eigenvalue.
</p>

</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_of_degeneracy_on_the_measurement_of_energy">Effect of degeneracy on the measurement of energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Effect of degeneracy on the measurement of energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(January 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In the absence of degeneracy, if a measured value of energy of a quantum system is determined, the corresponding state of the system is assumed to be known, since only one eigenstate corresponds to each energy eigenvalue. However, if the Hamiltonian <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {H}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<mi>H</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {H}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\hat {H}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6bb06de5217295d7fbdbf68fb9c5309a513fc99e" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.064ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> has a degenerate eigenvalue <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E_{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E_{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="E_{n}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ad6b82f2a00af6c9efd4c16d4e99329605645c0c" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.934ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> of degree g<sub>n</sub>, the eigenstates associated with it form a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vector_subspace" title="Vector subspace">vector subspace</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dimension" title="Dimension">dimension</a> g<sub>n</sub>. In such a case, several final states can be possibly associated with the same result <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E_{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E_{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="E_{n}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ad6b82f2a00af6c9efd4c16d4e99329605645c0c" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.934ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, all of which are linear combinations of the g<sub>n</sub> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthonormal" title="Orthonormal">orthonormal</a> eigenvectors <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |E_{n,i}\rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">⟩<!-- ⟩ --></mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle |E_{n,i}\rangle }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="|E_{n,i}\rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/54847c73125a86ee60f9a1034cbc847f7ed18dcc" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:5.51ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>In this case, the probability that the energy value measured for a system in the state <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |\psi \rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>ψ<!-- ψ --></mi>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">⟩<!-- ⟩ --></mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle |\psi \rangle }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="|\psi \rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cc27f1893b769a08cd6b296e115a29e61cab675e" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.065ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> will yield the value
<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E_{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E_{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="E_{n}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ad6b82f2a00af6c9efd4c16d4e99329605645c0c" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.934ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> is given by the sum of the probabilities of finding the system in each of the states in this basis, i.e.
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle P(E_{n})=\sum _{i=1}^{g_{n}}|\langle E_{n,i}|\psi \rangle |^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>P</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<munderover>
<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msub>
<mi>g</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mrow>
</munderover>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">⟨<!-- ⟨ --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mo>,</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>

</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P(E_{n})=\sum _{i=1}^{g_{n}}|\langle E_{n,i}|\psi \rangle |^{2}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="P(E_{n})=\sum _{i=1}^{g_{n}}|\langle E_{n,i}|\psi \rangle |^{2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d4a4a81696f30579204014aee4d96a909d1898a8" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:23.605ex; height:7.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Degeneracy_in_different_dimensions">Degeneracy in different dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Degeneracy in different dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This section intends to illustrate the existence of degenerate energy levels in quantum systems studied in different dimensions. The study of one and two-dimensional systems aids the conceptual understanding of more complex systems.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Degeneracy_in_one_dimension">Degeneracy in one dimension</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Degeneracy in one dimension">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In several cases, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Analytical_expression" title="Analytical expression">analytic</a> results can be obtained more easily in the study of one-dimensional systems. 
For a quantum particle with a wave function <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |\psi \rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>ψ<!-- ψ --></mi>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">⟩<!-- ⟩ --></mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle |\psi \rangle }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="|\psi \rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cc27f1893b769a08cd6b296e115a29e61cab675e" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.065ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> moving in a one-dimensional potential <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle V(x)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>V</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle V(x)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="V(x)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4ab3e825c2bf9c80d11d12e070a4626d48e03c61" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.926ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time-independent_Schr%C3%B6dinger_equation" title="Time-independent Schrödinger equation">time-independent Schrödinger equation</a> can be written as
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle -{\frac {\hbar ^{2}}{2m}}{\frac {d^{2}\psi }{dx^{2}}}+V\psi =E\psi }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<msup>
<mi class="MJX-variant">ℏ<!-- ℏ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mrow>
<mn>2</mn>
<mi>m</mi>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<msup>
<mi>d</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mi>ψ<!-- ψ --></mi>
</mrow>
<mrow>
<mi>d</mi>
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>V</mi>
<mi>ψ<!-- ψ --></mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>E</mi>
<mi>ψ<!-- ψ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle -{\frac {\hbar ^{2}}{2m}}{\frac {d^{2}\psi }{dx^{2}}}+V\psi =E\psi }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="-{\frac {\hbar ^{2}}{2m}}{\frac {d^{2}\psi }{dx^{2}}}+V\psi =E\psi " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d734054eed0bf9dd02eddbf52d565951b666af12" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:22.997ex; height:6.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Since this is an ordinary differential equation, there are two independent eigenfunctions for a given energy <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>E</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="E" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4232c9de2ee3eec0a9c0a19b15ab92daa6223f9b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.776ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> at most, so that the degree of degeneracy never exceeds two. 
It can be proved that in one dimension, there are no degenerate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bound_states" title="Bound states">bound states</a> for normalizable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wave_functions" title="Wave functions">wave functions</a>. A sufficient condition on a piecewise continuous potential <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle V}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>V</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle V}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="V" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/af0f6064540e84211d0ffe4dac72098adfa52845" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.787ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> and the energy <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>

<p>In case of well-defined and normalizable wave functions, the above constant vanishes, provided both the wave functions vanish at at least one point, and we find:
<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \psi _{1}(x)=c\psi _{2}(x)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>

<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \psi _{1}(x)=c\psi _{2}(x)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\psi _{1}(x)=c\psi _{2}(x)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3060245f4ccc1ce19c0f1e014d8d4fb58bfaebf0" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:15.518ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>
where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>c</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is, in general, a complex constant. For bound state <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eigenfunctions" title="Eigenfunctions">eigenfunctions</a> (which tend to zero as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x\rightarrow \infty }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x\rightarrow \infty }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x\rightarrow \infty " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/02579e74e2ef1ca0befceba816b311fe5bfd6844" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.268ex; height:1.843ex;"/></span>), and assuming <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle V}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>V</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="V" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/af0f6064540e84211d0ffe4dac72098adfa52845" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.787ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>E</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="E" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4232c9de2ee3eec0a9c0a19b15ab92daa6223f9b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.776ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> satisfy the condition given above, it can be shown<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-messiah1967_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-messiah1967-3">[3]</a></sup> that also the first derivative of the wave function approaches zero in the limit <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x\to \infty }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x\to \infty }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x\to \infty " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/eda2caf97ec29f30d5f0c0cd7135393361efc020" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.268ex; height:1.843ex;"/></span>, so that the above constant is zero and we have no degeneracy.
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Degeneracy_in_two-dimensional_quantum_systems">Degeneracy in two-dimensional quantum systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Degeneracy in two-dimensional quantum systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two-dimensional quantum systems exist in all three states of matter and much of the variety seen in three dimensional matter can be created in two dimensions. Real two-dimensional materials are made of monatomic layers on the surface of solids. Some examples of two-dimensional electron systems achieved experimentally include <a href="/wiki/MOSFET" title="MOSFET">MOSFET</a>, two-dimensional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superlattices" title="Superlattices">superlattices</a> of <a href="/wiki/Helium" title="Helium">Helium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neon" title="Neon">Neon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argon" title="Argon">Argon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xenon" title="Xenon">Xenon</a> etc. and surface of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liquid_Helium" title="Liquid Helium">liquid Helium</a>. 
The presence of degenerate energy levels is studied in the cases of particle in a box and two-dimensional <a href="/wiki/Harmonic_oscillator" title="Harmonic oscillator">harmonic oscillator</a>, which act as useful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mathematical_models" title="Mathematical models">mathematical models</a> for several real world systems.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Particle_in_a_rectangular_plane">Particle in a rectangular plane</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Particle in a rectangular plane">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n_{x},n_{y}=1,2,3...}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>So, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quantum_numbers" title="Quantum numbers">quantum numbers</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n_{x}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n_{x}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="n_{x}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2a811d9f1857b131167bd4238be8eb175ae3e85d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.567ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n_{y}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

<mi>n</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>y</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n_{y}}</annotation>
</semantics>

</p>

<p>For some commensurate ratios of the two lengths <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle L_{x}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Particle_in_a_square_box">Particle in a square box</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Particle in a square box">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In this case, the dimensions of the box <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle L_{x}=L_{y}=L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>Since <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n_{x}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

Degenerate states are also obtained when the sum of squares of quantum numbers corresponding to different energy levels are the same. For example, the three states (n<sub>x</sub> = 7, n<sub>y</sub> = 1), (n<sub>x</sub> = 1, n<sub>y</sub> = 7) and (n<sub>x</sub> = n<sub>y</sub> = 5) all have <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E=50{\frac {\pi ^{2}\hbar ^{2}}{2mL^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>Degrees of degeneracy of different energy levels for a particle in a square box
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finding_a_unique_eigenbasis_in_case_of_degeneracy">Finding a unique eigenbasis in case of degeneracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Finding a unique eigenbasis in case of degeneracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

However, if this eigenvalue, say <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>For two commuting observables <i>A</i> and <i>B</i>, one can construct an <a href="/wiki/Orthonormal_basis" title="Orthonormal basis">orthonormal basis</a> of the state space with eigenvectors common to the two operators. However, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\lambda " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b43d0ea3c9c025af1be9128e62a18fa74bedda2a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.355ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is a degenerate eigenvalue of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {A}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<mi>A</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {A}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\hat {A}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f595a6c73d1183d6a1b2ac21fe47ac28c1483821" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.776ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, then it is an eigensubspace of 
<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {A}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

<mover>
<mi>B</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {B}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\hat {B}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8ffa3bc40e590b7dfa0cd144e13163abf26e5c38" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.764ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>. However, it is always possible to choose, in every degenerate eigensubspace of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {A}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mover>
<mi>A</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Choosing_a_complete_set_of_commuting_observables">Choosing a complete set of commuting observables</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Choosing a complete set of commuting observables">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>If a given observable <i>A</i> is non-degenerate, there exists a unique basis formed by its eigenvectors. On the other hand, if one or several eigenvalues of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {A}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<mi>A</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {A}}}</annotation>
</semantics>

If, by choosing an observable <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {B}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

However, if a unique set of eigenvectors can still not be specified, for at least one of the pairs of eigenvalues, a third observable <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {C}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>It follows that the eigenfunctions of the Hamiltonian of a quantum system with a common energy value must be labelled by giving some additional information, which can be done by choosing an operator that commutes with the Hamiltonian.  These additional labels required naming of a unique energy eigenfunction and are usually related to the constants of motion of the system.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Degenerate_energy_eigenstates_and_the_parity_operator">Degenerate energy eigenstates and the parity operator</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Degenerate energy eigenstates and the parity operator">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The parity operator is defined by its action in the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |r\rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>r</mi>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">⟩<!-- ⟩ --></mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle |r\rangle }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="|r\rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b0599241b32d0e46ca7257fb0059cdd753fda9d5" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:2.6ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> representation of changing r to -r, i.e. 
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \langle r|P|\psi \rangle =\psi (-r)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>
<mi>P</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>ψ<!-- ψ --></mi>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">⟩<!-- ⟩ --></mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>ψ<!-- ψ --></mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>r</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \langle r|P|\psi \rangle =\psi (-r)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\langle r|P|\psi \rangle =\psi (-r)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/546cb9349c9b7b7beb4ad1692bd7ee762e43f9c7" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:16.688ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>The eigenvalues of P can be shown to be limited to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \pm 1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \pm 1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\pm 1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0bfeaa85da53ad1947d8000926cfea33827ef1e0" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.971ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, which are both degenerate eigenvalues in an infinite-dimensional state space. An eigenvector of P with eigenvalue +1 is said to be even, while that with eigenvalue −1 is said to be odd.
</p><p>Now, an even operator <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {A}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\tilde {A}}=P{\hat {A}}P}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>while an odd operator <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {B}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle P{\hat {B}}+{\hat {B}}P=0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P{\hat {B}}+{\hat {B}}P=0}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="P{\hat {B}}+{\hat {B}}P=0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d5442ce441064ce28dc575b3a6fa90c0c7ae28c5" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:14.12ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Since the square of the momentum operator <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {P}}^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<mi>P</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {P}}^{2}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\hat {P}}^{2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d4da4e507e9ad89c4de66cb0500ec8797ac17937" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.866ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span> is even, if the potential V(r) is even, the Hamiltonian <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {H}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<mi>H</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {H}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\hat {H}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6bb06de5217295d7fbdbf68fb9c5309a513fc99e" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.064ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> is said to be an even operator. In that case, if each of its eigenvalues are non-degenerate, each eigenvector is necessarily an eigenstate of P, and therefore it is possible to look for the eigenstates of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {H}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<mi>H</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {H}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\hat {H}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6bb06de5217295d7fbdbf68fb9c5309a513fc99e" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.064ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> among even and odd states. However, if one of the energy eigenstates has no definite <a href="/wiki/Parity_(physics)" title="Parity (physics)">parity</a>, it can be asserted that the corresponding eigenvalue is degenerate, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle P|\psi \rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>P</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>ψ<!-- ψ --></mi>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">⟩<!-- ⟩ --></mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P|\psi \rangle }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="P|\psi \rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a972c82a84a810d512995594fcffb858d1a7da8c" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.81ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> is an eigenvector of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {H}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<mi>H</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {H}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\hat {H}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6bb06de5217295d7fbdbf68fb9c5309a513fc99e" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.064ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> with the same eigenvalue as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |\psi \rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">⟩<!-- ⟩ --></mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle |\psi \rangle }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="|\psi \rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cc27f1893b769a08cd6b296e115a29e61cab675e" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.065ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Degeneracy_and_symmetry">Degeneracy and symmetry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Degeneracy and symmetry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The physical origin of degeneracy in a quantum-mechanical system is often the presence of some <a href="/wiki/Symmetry" title="Symmetry">symmetry</a> in the system. Studying the symmetry of a quantum system can, in some cases, enable us to find the energy levels and degeneracies without solving the Schrödinger equation, hence reducing effort.
</p><p>Mathematically, the relation of degeneracy with symmetry can be clarified as follows. Let us consider a <a href="/wiki/Symmetry_operation" title="Symmetry operation">symmetry operation</a> associated with a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_operator" title="Unitary operator">unitary operator</a> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span>. Under such an operation, the new Hamiltonian is related to the original Hamiltonian by a <a href="/wiki/Matrix_similarity" title="Matrix similarity">similarity transformation</a> generated by the operator <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span>, such that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H'=SHS^{-1}=SHS^{\dagger }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mo>′</mo>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>S</mi>
<mi>H</mi>
<msup>
<mi>S</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>S</mi>
<mi>H</mi>
<msup>
<mi>S</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>†<!-- † --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H'=SHS^{-1}=SHS^{\dagger }}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H'=SHS^{-1}=SHS^{\dagger }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/44e3124d7e8aaa0c572c8229224993cc95729400" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:22.449ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>, since <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span> is unitary. If the Hamiltonian remains unchanged under the transformation operation <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span>, we have

<p>Now, if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |\alpha \rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H|\alpha \rangle =E|\alpha \rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>where E is the corresponding energy eigenvalue.
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle HS|\alpha \rangle =SH|\alpha \rangle =SE|\alpha \rangle =ES|\alpha \rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

If the two states <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |\alpha \rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>In cases where <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span> is characterized by a continuous <a href="/wiki/Parameter" title="Parameter">parameter</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \epsilon }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<semantics>

<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>

<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>

<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">⟩<!-- ⟩ --></mo>
</mstyle>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="S(\epsilon )|\alpha \rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c95f810c58002763e0420d24535257721d8d3a34" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:7.292ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> have the same energy eigenvalue.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symmetry_group_of_the_Hamiltonian">Symmetry group of the Hamiltonian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Symmetry group of the Hamiltonian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The set of all operators which commute with the Hamiltonian of a quantum system are said to form the <a href="/wiki/Symmetry_group" title="Symmetry group">symmetry group</a> of the Hamiltonian. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commutators" title="Commutators">commutators</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Generator_(groups)" title="Generator (groups)">generators</a> of this group determine the <a href="/wiki/Algebra" title="Algebra">algebra</a> of the group. An n-dimensional representation of the Symmetry group preserves the <a href="/wiki/Multiplication_table" title="Multiplication table">multiplication table</a> of the symmetry operators. The possible degeneracies of the Hamiltonian with a particular symmetry group are given by the dimensionalities of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irreducible_representations" title="Irreducible representations">irreducible representations</a> of the group. The eigenfunctions corresponding to a n-fold degenerate eigenvalue form a basis for a n-dimensional irreducible representation of the Symmetry group of the Hamiltonian.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_degeneracy">Types of degeneracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Types of degeneracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Degeneracies in a quantum system can be systematic or accidental in nature.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Systematic_or_essential_degeneracy">Systematic or essential degeneracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Systematic or essential degeneracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This is also called a geometrical or normal degeneracy and arises due to the presence of some kind of symmetry in the system under consideration, i.e. the invariance of the Hamiltonian under a certain operation, as described above. The representation obtained from a normal degeneracy is irreducible and the corresponding eigenfunctions form a basis for this representation.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidental_degeneracy">Accidental degeneracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Accidental degeneracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It is a type of degeneracy resulting from some special features of the system or the functional form of the potential under consideration, and is related possibly to a hidden dynamical symmetry in the system. It also results in conserved quantities, which are often not easy to identify. Accidental symmetries lead to these additional degeneracies in the discrete energy spectrum. An accidental degeneracy can be due to the fact that the group of the Hamiltonian is not complete. These degeneracies are connected to the existence of bound orbits in classical Physics.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Examples_of_systems_with_accidental_degeneracies">Examples of systems with accidental degeneracies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Examples of systems with accidental degeneracies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Coulomb_and_Harmonic_Oscillator_potentials">The Coulomb and Harmonic Oscillator potentials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: The Coulomb and Harmonic Oscillator potentials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For a particle in a central 1/r potential, the <a href="/wiki/Laplace%E2%80%93Runge%E2%80%93Lenz_vector" title="Laplace–Runge–Lenz vector">Laplace–Runge–Lenz vector</a> is a conserved quantity resulting from an accidental degeneracy, in addition to the conservation of <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum" title="Angular momentum">angular momentum</a> due to rotational invariance.
</p><p>For a particle moving on a cone under the influence of 1/r and r<sup>2</sup> potentials, centred at the tip of the cone, the conserved quantities corresponding to accidental symmetry will be two components of an equivalent of the Runge-Lenz vector, in addition to one component of the angular momentum vector. These quantities generate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SU(2)" title="SU(2)">SU(2)</a> symmetry for both potentials.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Particle_in_a_constant_magnetic_field">Particle in a constant magnetic field</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Particle in a constant magnetic field">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A particle moving under the influence of a constant magnetic field, undergoing <a href="/wiki/Cyclotron" title="Cyclotron">cyclotron</a> motion on a circular orbit is another important example of an accidental symmetry. The symmetry <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiplets" title="Multiplets">multiplets</a> in this case are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landau_levels" title="Landau levels">Landau levels</a> which are infinitely degenerate.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Examples">Examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Examples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_hydrogen_atom">The hydrogen atom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: The hydrogen atom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_atom" title="Hydrogen atom">Hydrogen Atom</a></div>

</p><p>The degeneracy with respect to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle m_{l}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle m_{l}}</annotation>
</semantics>

The degeneracy with respect to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle l}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>l</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle l}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="l" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/829091f745070b9eb97a80244129025440a1cfac" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.693ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is often described as an accidental degeneracy, but it can be explained in terms of special symmetries of the Schrödinger equation which are only valid for the hydrogen atom in which the potential energy is given by <a href="/wiki/Coulomb%27s_law" title="Coulomb's law">Coulomb's law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merzbacher98_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Merzbacher98-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 267f</span></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Isotropic_three-dimensional_harmonic_oscillator">Isotropic three-dimensional harmonic oscillator</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Isotropic three-dimensional harmonic oscillator">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It is a spinless <a href="/wiki/Particle" title="Particle">particle</a> of mass m moving in <a href="/wiki/Three-dimensional_space" title="Three-dimensional space">three-dimensional space</a>, subject to a <a href="/wiki/Central_force" title="Central force">central force</a> whose absolute value is proportional to the distance of the particle from the centre of force. 
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle F=-kr}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<p>Only the ground state is non-degenerate.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Removing_degeneracy">Removing degeneracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Removing degeneracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The degeneracy in a quantum mechanical system may be removed if the underlying symmetry is broken by an external <a href="/wiki/Perturbation_theory_(quantum_mechanics)" title="Perturbation theory (quantum mechanics)">perturbation</a>. This causes splitting in the degenerate energy levels. This is essentially a splitting of the original irreducible representations into lower-dimensional such representations of the perturbed system.
</p><p>Mathematically, the splitting due to the application of a small perturbation potential can be calculated using time-independent degenerate <a href="/wiki/Perturbation_theory" title="Perturbation theory">perturbation theory</a>. This is an approximation scheme that can be applied to find the solution to the eigenvalue equation for the Hamiltonian H of a quantum system with an applied perturbation, given the solution for the Hamiltonian H<sub>0</sub> for the unperturbed system. It involves expanding the eigenvalues and eigenkets of the Hamiltonian H in a perturbation series.  
The degenerate eigenstates with a given energy eigenvalue form a vector subspace, but not every basis of eigenstates of this space is a good starting point for perturbation theory, because typically there would not be any eigenstates of the perturbed system near them. The correct basis to choose is one that diagonalizes the perturbation Hamiltonian within the degenerate subspace.
</p>
<dl><dd><table class="toccolours collapsible collapsed" style="text-align:left" width="60%">
<tbody><tr>
<th>Lifting of degeneracy by first-order degenerate perturbation theory.
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>Consider an unperturbed Hamiltonian <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {H_{0}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<msub>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_examples_of_removal_of_degeneracy_by_a_perturbation">Physical examples of removal of degeneracy by a perturbation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Physical examples of removal of degeneracy by a perturbation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some important examples of physical situations where degenerate energy levels of a quantum system are split by the application of an external perturbation are given below.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symmetry_breaking_in_two-level_systems">Symmetry breaking in two-level systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Symmetry breaking in two-level systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Two-level_system" title="Two-level system">two-level system</a> essentially refers to a physical system having two states whose energies are close together and very different from those of the other states of the system. All calculations for such a system are performed on a two-dimensional <a href="/wiki/Subspace_topology" title="Subspace topology">subspace</a> of the state space.
</p><p>If the ground state of a physical system is two-fold degenerate, any coupling between the two corresponding states lowers the energy of the ground state of the system, and makes it more stable.
</p><p>If <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E_{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E_{1}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="E_{1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7ac42446bcd2cbb76ec8fe2895635d328da22e26" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.769ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E_{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E_{2}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="E_{2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8e6ee346e54f38302f47b5cf3016d8718f2040c0" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.769ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> are the energy levels of the system, such that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E_{1}=E_{2}=E}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>E</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>E</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E_{1}=E_{2}=E}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="E_{1}=E_{2}=E" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/faf3df2330c3d04e9828d6836db035a3c15ece44" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:13.511ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, and the perturbation <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle W}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>W</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle W}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="W" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/54a9c4c547f4d6111f81946cad242b18298d70b7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.435ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is represented in the two-dimensional subspace as the following 2×2 matrix
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {W} ={\begin{bmatrix}0&amp;W_{12}\\W_{12}^{*}&amp;0\end{bmatrix}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">W</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow>
<mo>[</mo>
<mtable columnspacing="1em" rowspacing="4pt">
<mtr>
<mtd>
<mn>0</mn>
</mtd>
<mtd>
<msub>
<mi>W</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>12</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mtd>
</mtr>
<mtr>
<mtd>
<msubsup>

<mn>12</mn>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</mrow>
</msubsup>
</mtd>
<mtd>
<mn>0</mn>
</mtd>
</mtr>
</mtable>
<mo>]</mo>
</mrow>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {W} ={\begin{bmatrix}0&amp;W_{12}\\W_{12}^{*}&amp;0\end{bmatrix}}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf {W} ={\begin{bmatrix}0&amp;W_{12}\\W_{12}^{*}&amp;0\end{bmatrix}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2484a2fc586f9e45b996b42e787de93b2829f950" style="vertical-align: -2.332ex; margin-bottom: -0.173ex; width:20.177ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>then the perturbed energies are
</p>
