<p>Examples of two-state systems in which the degeneracy in energy states is broken by the presence of off-diagonal terms in the Hamiltonian resulting from an internal interaction due to an inherent property of the system include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Benzene" title="Benzene">Benzene</a>, with two possible dispositions of the three double bonds between neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">Carbon</a> atoms.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">Ammonia</a> molecule, where the Nitrogen atom can be either above or below the plane defined by the three <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">Hydrogen</a> atoms.</li>
<li><span class="chemf nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Dihydrogen_cation" title="Dihydrogen cation">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></a></span> molecule, in which the electron may be localized around either of the two nuclei.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine-structure_splitting">Fine-structure splitting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Fine-structure splitting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The corrections to the Coulomb interaction between the electron and the proton in a Hydrogen atom due to relativistic motion and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spin-orbit_coupling" title="Spin-orbit coupling">spin-orbit coupling</a> result in breaking the degeneracy in energy levels for different values of l corresponding to a single principal quantum number n.
</p><p>The perturbation Hamiltonian due to relativistic correction is given by
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H_{r}=-p^{4}/8m^{3}c^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zeeman_effect">Zeeman effect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Zeeman effect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The splitting of the energy levels of an atom when placed in an external magnetic field because of the interaction of the <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_moment" title="Magnetic moment">magnetic moment</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\vec {m}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<mi>m</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\vec {m}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\vec {m}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/24e08685bde682d6b67c3a22b026d16dbbf8dfcc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.04ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> of the atom with the applied field is known as the <a href="/wiki/Zeeman_effect" title="Zeeman effect">Zeeman effect</a>.
</p><p>Taking into consideration the orbital and spin angular momenta, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\vec {L}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>

<mo>/</mo>

<mi>m</mi>

</semantics>

Thus,

<p>Now, in case of the weak-field Zeeman effect, when the applied field is weak compared to the internal field, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spin-orbit_coupling" title="Spin-orbit coupling">spin-orbit coupling</a> dominates and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\vec {L}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lifting_of_degeneracy_(energy_level_diagram).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="460" data-file-width="819" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Lifting_of_degeneracy_%28energy_level_diagram%29.png/220px-Lifting_of_degeneracy_%28energy_level_diagram%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Lifting_of_degeneracy_%28energy_level_diagram%29.png/330px-Lifting_of_degeneracy_%28energy_level_diagram%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Lifting_of_degeneracy_%28energy_level_diagram%29.png/440px-Lifting_of_degeneracy_%28energy_level_diagram%29.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lifting_of_degeneracy_(energy_level_diagram).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lifting of degeneracy by an external magnetic field</div></div></div>
<p>In case of the strong-field Zeeman effect, when the applied field is strong enough, so that the orbital and spin angular momenta decouple, the good quantum numbers are now n,l,m<sub>l</sub> and m<sub>s</sub>. Here, L<sub>z</sub> and S<sub>z</sub> are conserved, so the perturbation Hamiltonian is given by-

<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {V}}=eB(L_{z}+2S_{z})/2m}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>2</mn>
<msub>
<mi>S</mi>

</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\hat {V}}=eB(m_{l}+2m_{s})/2m}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>For each value of m<sub>l</sub>, there are two possible values of m<sub>s</sub>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \pm 1/2}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stark_effect">Stark effect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degenerate_energy_levels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Stark effect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The splitting of the energy levels of an atom or molecule when subjected to an external electric field is known as the <a href="/wiki/Stark_effect" title="Stark effect">Stark effect</a>.
</p><p>For the hydrogen atom, the perturbation Hamiltonian is-

</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle m_{l}=m_{l1}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="m_{l}=m_{l1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cc0ff065ada198fed8c698ff955cdb1cc2e51b54" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:9.446ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>The degeneracy is lifted only for certain states obeying the selection rules, in the first order. The first-order splitting in the energy levels for the degenerate states <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |2,0,0\rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
